To help determine the effect of such a restricted environment on their microflora, an extensive evaluation of the microbial load\nof eachastronaut was conductedwithin 5 hours before launch andwithin 2 hours following recovery. All postflight sample analyseswere conductedwithin class III biological\ncabinetry of the LRL (fig. 4) to avoid possible introduction of lunar contaminants\ninto the terrestrial biosphere.\nImmediately after recovery, the crewmembers entered the sickbay aboard the\nU.S.S. NewOrleans at which time microbiological specimenswere obtained. These\nspecimens were returned to MSCwhere microbial loads were studied. facility.Prior\nto crew entry\ninto the MQF, four sites\n(sink,\ntable,\nfloor,\nand telephone)\nwere sampled.\nThese\nsamples\nwere packed\nin ice\nand returned\nto the MSC, where\nthey were the MSC.\nClose contact\nwithin an extremely\nconfined\narea made microbial\ninterchange\npossible.\nThe MQF personnel\nwere screened\nfor the\npresence\nof medically\nimportant\nmicroorganisms\nbefore\ncrew contact,\nand again at the\nend of the isolation\nperiod\n(table XXXVII).\nComparison\nof these\ndata allowed\nevaluation of microbial\ninterchange.\nStaphylococcus\naureus\nisolates\nwere recovered\nprior\nto quarantine\nfrom three\ndifferent\nflight surgeon\nsamples\nand from four different\nengineer\nsamples.\nAfter 18 days\nof quarantine\n, S. aureus\nwas recovered\nfrom only one site oneach\nsubject.\nPhage\ntyping of these preand postquarantine\nisolates\ndemonstrated\ntotal host specificity;\nthe\nisolates\nfrom one subject\nwere all type 53/77,\nwhereas\nthose from the other\nsubject\nwere all untypable\n(table XXXVIII).\nOther\nisolates\nof special\ninterest\nincluded\nthose recovered\nfrom\nthe pseudomonad\nfrom the stool specimen\nof the flight surgeon.\nEither\nmicrobial\ntypes could have contributed\nto a serious\nillness\nevent.\n\nthe urine and\none of these\n\nThe crew reception\narea.On arrival\nat the Manned\nSpacecraft\nCenter,\nthe astronauts and MQF personnel\nwere transferred\nfrom the MQF to the Crew Reception\nArea\nof the Lunar\nReceiving\nLaboratory.\nNasal swabs,\nthroat\nswabs,\nand fecal\nsamples\nwere collected\nfrom each of the 12 people\nwho would come in contact\nwith the astronauts during\ntheir\nstay in the CRA.\nNasal\nswab samples\nand throat\nswab samples\nwere\nagain obtained\nfrom the 12 CRA personnel\nat the end of the 16-day quarantine\nperiod.\nComparison\nof the medically\nimportant\nmicrobial\nload recovered\nfrom these\ntwo sampling periods\nwas required\nin order\nto monitor\nmicrobial\ninterchange\nduring this period.\nNo /3-hemolytic streptococci were isolated from CRA personnel before postflight\nquarantine. However, on release from isolation,_-hemolytic Streptococcus sp. (not\ngroup A) was isolated from one throat culture. This could have resulted from the introduction of astronauts A and B into the environment as both carried this microorganism in their upper respiratory tracts. It is equally possible, however, that fl-hemolytic\nstreptococci were present in unsampled areas of the CRA personnel and were transferred to the throat independent of astronaut contact.\nStaphylococcus\naureus\nwas recovered\nfrom one-third\nof the CRA personnel\nduring\nboth sampling\nperiods.\nPhage typing (table XXXVIII) of these\nmicrobes\ndemonstrated\nthat those recovered\nafter\nquarantine\nisolation\nwere different\nin all cases\nfrom those\nrecovered\nbefore\nquarantine\nisolation.\nAnalyses\nof the phage type pattern\nof all S. aureus\ncultures\nobtained\npostflight\n(table XXXVIII) fail to indicate\nany possibility\nof microbial\ninterchange\nof this microorganism\nin the CRA quarantine\nenvironment.\n\n18\n\nCONCLUDING\n\nREMARKS\n\nThe data presented\nin this report\nare based\non analyses\nof 12_ different\nsample:\nfrom each of the three prime\ncrewmembers\nfor each of the five sal:lple\nperiods.\nSe_\neral observations,\n25 of which are listed\nin the following,\nmay be ,__ncluded\nfrom _h\ndata presented\nin this report.\nResponses\n13 to 25 were indicated\nf_om immediate\npostflight\nsample\ndata.\n1.
